# Architecture Q&A: Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline

**Repository:** hashicorp/terraform
**Task Type:** Architecture Q&A (investigation only — no code changes)

## Background

Terraform's `terraform plan` command builds a dependency graph of all resources in the configuration, resolves providers, and computes the diff between desired state and current state. This process involves multiple layers: CLI command parsing, backend operation execution, graph construction via a series of transformers, concurrent graph walking, and provider plugin communication for diff computation.

## Questions

Answer ALL of the following questions about Terraform's plan execution pipeline:

### Q1: Command to Context

When a user runs `terraform plan`, how does the CLI command reach the core planning logic? Specifically:
- How does `PlanCommand.Run()` in `internal/command/plan.go` delegate to the backend?
- How does the backend create and invoke `terraform.Context.Plan()`?
- What are the key fields of `PlanOpts` that control plan behavior (mode, targets, force-replace)?

### Q2: Graph Construction Pipeline

How does `PlanGraphBuilder` construct the dependency graph for a plan operation?
- What is the role of the `Steps()` method and how does the sequence of `GraphTransformer` stages build the graph?
- Specifically, what do `ConfigTransformer`, `ReferenceTransformer`, and `AttachStateTransformer` each contribute?
- How does `ReferenceTransformer` analyze node references to add dependency edges between resources?

### Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration

How are providers resolved, initialized, and configured during the plan walk?
- How does `EvalContext.InitProvider()` instantiate a provider plugin?
- At what point in graph execution is `ConfigureProvider()` called relative to resource planning?
- What is the role of `CloseProviderTransformer` in the graph lifecycle?

### Q4: Diff Computation per Resource

For a single managed resource instance, how does Terraform compute the planned changes?
- Trace the execution path from `NodePlannableResourceInstance.Execute()` through `managedResourceExecute()`
- How does the refresh phase (`refresh()`) synchronize with remote state before planning?
- How does the `plan()` method invoke the provider's `PlanResourceChange` RPC to compute the diff?
- What determines whether a resource is marked for create, update, replace, or delete?

## Output Requirements

Write your answer to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with the following structure:


- Cite specific files, types, and functions — avoid vague or speculative answers
- Focus on the `internal/terraform/`, `internal/command/`, and `internal/providers/` directories

    16→// PlanCommand is a Command implementation that compares a Terraform
    17→// configuration to an actual infrastructure and shows the differences.
    18→type PlanCommand struct {
    19→	Meta
    20→}
    21→
    22→func (c *PlanCommand) Run(rawArgs []string) int {
    23→	// Parse and apply global view arguments
    24→	common, rawArgs := arguments.ParseView(rawArgs)
    25→	c.View.Configure(common)
    26→
    27→	// Propagate -no-color for legacy use of Ui.  The remote backend and
    28→	// cloud package use this; it should be removed when/if they are
    29→	// migrated to views.
    30→	c.Meta.color = !common.NoColor
    31→	c.Meta.Color = c.Meta.color
    32→
    33→	// Parse and validate flags
    34→	args, diags := arguments.ParsePlan(rawArgs)
    35→
    36→	// Instantiate the view, even if there are flag errors, so that we render
    37→	// diagnostics according to the desired view
    38→	view := views.NewPlan(args.ViewType, c.View)
    39→
    40→	if diags.HasErrors() {
    41→		view.Diagnostics(diags)
    42→		view.HelpPrompt()
    43→		return 1
    44→	}
    45→
    46→	// Check for user-supplied plugin path
    47→	var err error
    48→	if c.pluginPath, err = c.loadPluginPath(); err != nil {
    49→		diags = diags.Append(err)
    50→		view.Diagnostics(diags)
    51→		return 1
    52→	}

   120→func (c *PlanCommand) PrepareBackend(args *arguments.State, viewType arguments.ViewType) (backendrun.OperationsBackend, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {
   121→	// FIXME: we need to apply the state arguments to the meta object here
   122→	// because they are later used when initializing the backend. Carving a
   123→	// path to pass these arguments to the functions that need them is
   124→	// difficult but would make their use easier to understand.
   125→	c.Meta.applyStateArguments(args)
   126→
   127→	backendConfig, diags := c.loadBackendConfig(".")
   128→	if diags.HasErrors() {
   129→		return nil, diags
   130→	}
   131→
   132→	// Load the backend
   133→	be, beDiags := c.Backend(&BackendOpts{
   134→		Config:   backendConfig,
   135→		ViewType: viewType,
   136→	})
   137→	diags = diags.Append(beDiags)
   138→	if beDiags.HasErrors() {
   139→		return nil, diags
   140→	}
   141→
   142→	return be, diags
   143→}

    18→// PlanGraphBuilder is a GraphBuilder implementation that builds a graph for
    19→// planning and for other "plan-like" operations which don't require an
    20→// already-calculated plan as input.
    21→//
    22→// Unlike the apply graph builder, this graph builder:
    23→//
    24→//   - Makes its decisions primarily based on the given configuration, which
    25→//     represents the desired state.
    26→//
    27→//   - Ignores certain lifecycle concerns like create_before_destroy, because
    28→//     those are only important once we already know what action we're planning
    29→//     to take against a particular resource instance.
    30→type PlanGraphBuilder struct {
    31→	// Config is the configuration tree to build a plan from.
    32→	Config *configs.Config
    33→
    34→	// State is the current state
    35→	State *states.State
    36→
    37→	// RootVariableValues are the raw input values for root input variables
    38→	// given by the caller, which we'll resolve into final values as part
    39→	// of the plan walk.
    40→	RootVariableValues InputValues
    41→
    42→	// ExternalProviderConfigs are pre-initialized root module provider
    43→	// configura
... (truncated)

    14→// GraphBuilder is an interface that can be implemented and used with
    15→// Terraform to build the graph that Terraform walks.
    16→type GraphBuilder interface {
    17→	// Build builds the graph for the given module path. It is up to
    18→	// the interface implementation whether this build should expand
    19→	// the graph or not.
    20→	Build(addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics)
    21→}
    22→
    23→// BasicGraphBuilder is a GraphBuilder that builds a graph out of a
    24→// series of transforms and (optionally) validates the graph is a valid
    25→// structure.
    26→type BasicGraphBuilder struct {
    27→	Steps []GraphTransformer
    28→	// Optional name to add to the graph debug log
    29→	Name string
    30→}
    31→
    32→func (b *BasicGraphBuilder) Build(path addrs.ModuleInstance) (*Graph, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {
    33→	var diags tfdiags.Diagnostics
    34→	g := &Graph{Path: path}
    35→
    36→	var lastStepStr string
    37→	for _, step := range b.Steps {
    38→		if step == nil {
    39→			continue
    40→		}
    41→		log.Printf("[TRACE] Executing graph transform %T", step)
    42→
    43→		err := step.Transform(g)
    44→		if thisStepStr := g.StringWithNodeTypes(); thisStepStr != lastStepStr {
    45→			log.Printf("[TRACE] Completed graph transform %T with new graph:\n%s  ------", step, logging.Indent(thisStepStr))
    46→			lastStepStr = thisStepStr
    47→		} else {
    4

   121→func (b *PlanGraphBuilder) Steps() []GraphTransformer {

   108→// ReferenceTransformer is a GraphTransformer that connects all the
   109→// nodes that reference each other in order to form the proper ordering.
   110→type ReferenceTransformer struct{}
   111→
   112→func (t *ReferenceTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {
   113→	// Build a reference map so we can efficiently look up the references
   114→	vs := g.Vertices()
   115→	m := NewReferenceMap(vs)
   116→
   117→	// Find the things that reference things and connect them
   118→	for _, v := range vs {
   119→		if _, ok := v.(GraphNodeDestroyer); ok {
   120→			// destroy nodes references are not connected, since they can only
   121→			// use their own state.
   122→			continue
   123→		}
   124→
   125→		parents := m.References(v)
   126→		parentsDbg := make([]string, len(parents))
   127→		for i, v := range parents {
   128→			parentsDbg[i] = dag.VertexName(v)
   129→		}
   130→		log.Printf(
   131→			"[DEBUG] ReferenceTransformer: %q references: %v",
   132→			dag.VertexName(v), parentsDbg)
   133→
   134→		for _, parent := range parents {
   135→			// A destroy plan relies solely on the state, so we only need to
   136→			// ensure that temporary values are connected to get the evaluation
   137→			// order correct. Any references to destroy nodes will cause
   138→			// cycles, because they are connected in reverse order.
   139→			if _, ok := parent.(GraphNodeDestroyer)
... (truncated)

   257→func (t *CloseProviderTransformer) Transform(g *Graph) error {
   258→	pm := providerVertexMap(g)
   259→	cpm := make(map[string]*graphNodeCloseProvider)
   260→	var err error
   261→
   262→	for _, p := range pm {
   263→		key := p.ProviderAddr().String()
   264→
   265→		// make sure we haven't created the closer node already
   266→		_, ok := cpm[key]
   267→		if ok {
   268→			log.Printf("[ERROR] CloseProviderTransformer: already created close node for %s", key)
   269→			continue
   270→		}
   271→
   272→		// create a closer for this provider type
   273→		closer := &graphNodeCloseProvider{Addr: p.ProviderAddr()}
   274→		g.Add(closer)
   275→		cpm[key] = closer
   276→
   277→		// Close node depends on the provider itself
   278→		// this is added unconditionally, so it will connect to all instances
   279→		// of the provider. Extra edges will be removed by transitive
   280→		// reduction.
   281→		g.Connect(dag.BasicEdge(closer, p))
   282→	}
   283→
   284→	// Now look for all provider consumers and connect them to the appropriate closers.
   285→	for _, v := range g.Vertices() {
   286→		pc, ok := v.(GraphNodeProviderConsumer)
   287→		if !ok {
   288→			continue
   289→		}
   290→
   291→		p, exact := pc.ProvidedBy()
   292→		if p == nil && exact {
   293→			// this node does not require a provider
   294→			continue
   295→		}
   296→
   297→		provider, ok := p.(addrs.AbsProviderConfig)
   298→		if !ok {
   299→			return fmt.Errorf("%s failed to return a provider reference", dag.VertexName(pc))
   300→		}
   301→
   302→		closer, ok := cpm[provider.String()]
   303→		if !ok {
   304→			return fmt.Errorf("no graphNodeCloseProvider for %s", provider)
   305→		}

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of Terraform's plan/apply pipeline architecture. Here's a summary of what I've documented:

## Investigation Summary

I've written a detailed architectural analysis to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` covering all four questions:

### **Q1: Command to Context**
Traced the execution flow from `PlanCommand.Run()` → `PrepareBackend()` → `OperationRequest()` → `RunOperation()` → `Context.Plan()`. Detailed how PlanOpts fields (Mode, Targets, ForceReplace, SkipRefresh, DeferralAllowed) control plan behavior.

### **Q2: Graph Construction Pipeline**
Documented the **27-step transformer sequence** that builds the dependency graph:
- **ConfigTransformer**: Adds resource nodes from configuration
- **ReferenceTransformer**: Analyzes expression references and creates dependency edges by building a reference map and connecting nodes based on what they reference
- **AttachStateTransformer**: Attaches current state objects to resource instance nodes for access during planning

The transformers execute in a specific sequence to progressively build the graph, with reference resolution happening after all nodes are created.

### **Q3: Provider Resolution and Configuration**
- **InitProvider()**: Instantiates provider plugins via the plugin system, with special handling for external pre-configured providers
- **ConfigureProvider()**: Evaluates provider blocks, validates configuration, and sends configuration to provider via `ConfigureProvider()` RPC
- **CloseProviderTransformer**: Creates cleanup nodes that execute after all resource usage completes

### **Q4: Diff Computation per Resource**
Traced the complete flow for a managed resource:

1. **Refresh Phase** (if not skipped): Calls `provider.ReadResource()` RPC with prior state to det

Schema** (lines 758-768):\n   - `getProvider()` retrieves configured provider\n   - Gets provider schema for the resource type\n\n2. **Configuration Evaluation** (lines 819-832):\n   - 884-888):\n   - Applies `ignore_changes` to prevent spurious diffs\n   - Removes configured attributes from comparison\n\n4. **Value Preparation** (lines 890-896):\n   - Unmarked values for sending to provider\n   - Creates `proposedNewVal` from prior state + config\n   - Uses `objchange.ProposedNew()` logic\n\n5. **Pre-diff Hook** (lines 899-904):\n   - Calls UI hook with prior/proposed values\n\n6. **Provider PlanResourceChange RPC** (lines 927-937):\n   ```go\n   resp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n       TypeName: n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n       Config: unmarkedConfigVal,\n       PriorState: unmarkedPriorVal,\n       ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n       PriorPrivate: priorPrivate,\n Determination** (lines 1048-1141):\n\n   **Helper Function:** `getAction()` (defined in file, used line 1054)\n\n   ```go\n   action, actionReason := getAction(\n       n.Addr, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedPlannedNewVal,\n       createBeforeDestroy, forceReplace, reqRep\n   )\n   ```\n\n   Determines action based on:\n   - Prior state is null \u2192 **Create**\n   - Planned state equals prior state \u2192 **NoOp**\n   - Provider's `RequiresReplace` paths differ \u2192 **Replace**\n   - User's `-replace=` matches instance \u2192 **Replace** (overrides)\n   - create_before_destroy flag \u2192 **CreateThenDelete** or **DeleteThenCreate**\n\n   If action is **Replace**:\n   - Calls `provider.PlanResourceChange()` again with null prior state\n   - Gets clean creation plan without computed fields from destroyed instance\n   - Merges with actual prior for accurate before/after representation\n\n9. **Tainted Resource Handling** (lines 1146-1154):\n   - If prior state was tainted, - Calls UI hook with final action and values\n\n12. **Change Object Creation** (lines 1191+):\n    - Creates `plans.ResourceInstanceChange` with:\n      - `Addr`: Resource address\n      - `Action`: Determined action\n      - `Before`: Prior state value\n      - `After`: Planned state value\n      - Marks and metadata\n\n### Action Determination Logic\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n\n**Function:** `getAction()` (line 2736)\n\nPseudo-algorithm:\n\n```\nif priorVal.IsNull():\n    return Create\nelif plannedNewVal.Equal(priorVal):\n    if forceReplace contains this instance:\n        return Replace\n    elif requiredReplaces is not empty:\n        return Replace\n    else:\n        return NoOp\nelse:\n    if requiredReplaces is not empty:\n        return Replace\n    else:\n        return Update\n```\n\nThe `requiredReplaces` set comes from provider's `RequiresReplace` response, indicating which attributes changed in a way requiring deletion.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Key File Paths and Line References\n\n**Command Layer:**\n- `internal/command/plan.go:22` - PlanCommand.Run() # Terraform Plan/Apply Pipeline Architecture

## Q1: Command to Context

### CLI Command Parsing and Backend Delegation

**File:** `internal/command/plan.go`

The `PlanCommand.Run()` method (line 22) is the entry point for the `terraform plan` CLI command. The command processing flow:

1. **Argument Parsing** (lines 24-44):
   - `arguments.ParseView()` - parses global view arguments
   - `arguments.ParsePlan()` - parses plan-specific flags
   - Creates a `views.Plan` to render diagnostics

2. **Backend Preparation** (line 68):
   - `PrepareBackend()` loads the backend and returns a `backendrun.OperationsBackend` interface

3. **Operation Request Building** (line 82):
   - `OperationRequest()` constructs the operation request with:
     - `args.PlanMode` → `opReq.PlanMode`
     - `args.Targets` → `opReq.Targets`
     - `args.ForceReplace` → `opReq.ForceReplace`
     - `args.Refresh` → `opReq.PlanRefresh`
     - `args.DeferralAllowed` → `opReq.DeferralAllowed`

4. **Variable Collection** (line 90):
   - `GatherVariables()` collects user-supplied variable values

5. **Backend Operation Execution** (line 103):
   - `RunOperation()` delegates to the backend which implements the operation protocol

### Backend to Context Delegation

**File:** `internal/backend/local/backend_plan.go`

The backend's plan operation (`opPlan`, line 23) manages the overall plan process:

1. **Context Creation** (line 80):
   - `localRun()` prepares a `backendrun.LocalRun` which contains:
     - The `terraform.Context` instance
     - The loaded configuration
     - The input state
     - The `PlanOpts` (prepared in `localRunDirect`, lines 142-222)

2. **Plan Options Construction** (`localRunDirect`, lines 200-209):
   - Creates `terraform.PlanOpts` with:
     - `Mode`: Normal, Destroy, or RefreshO
... (truncated)
